Compressor bleed air is available for pressurization, heating and ventilation  of the T-44C cabin. This bleed air is   tapped off of the diffuser section just  after the 4th stage compressor and prior to the combustion chamber. Because the bleed air is delivered to the cabin at a relatively constant rate, the pressurization system controls the T-44C cabin pressure by controlling the outflow of air from the cabin through two (2) flow control valves (the outflow valve and the safety valve). ","roles":{"textData":{}}},{"id":"Slide107677","class":"Normal Slide","instance":"t02p025","thumbnail":"","children":["si158832","Click_Box_377","Image_2119","Text_Caption_6752","Widget_22"],"roles":{"slide":{"durationInFrames":90},"navigation":{"navid":"Slide107677"}}},{"id":"si159180","class":"TODO::Senthil","roles":{"click":{"subtype":"button"},"question":{"interactionId":"183235","quizId":-1,"text":"Image ","type":"graded","interactionType":"choice","score":{"weight":1,"penalty":0}},"textData":{}}},{"id":"Click_Box_721","class":"TODO::Senthil","instance":"Click_Box_721","roles":{"click":{"subtype":"button"}}},{"id":"Text_Caption_6150","class":"TODO::Senthil","instance":"Text_Caption_6150","title":"Safety Valve  The safety valve is also located on the aft pressure bulkhead near the outflow valve.   The safety valve is connected to the cabin pressure control switch and is wired through the left landing gear squat switch.   When the control switch is set to DUMP (or the LH squat switch is closed and the switch is set to PRESS), the safety valve serves as a dump valve. This means it completely opens to relieve all the pressure differential between the external air pressure and the cabin air pressure. So, for smoke and fume elimination, going to dump would allow ram scoop ambient air to flow though the cabin, flushing the fumes out via the safety valve.   A second function of the safety valve is  to back up the outflow valve. The safety valve also contains a preadjusted relief valve. This valve is set to ensure that differential pressure does not exceed  4.9 psi. (Careful, this is easy to confuse with the preadjusted valve in the outflow valve.) After the engine(s) are started, the compressor bleed air is tapped off  the manifold at a T-fitting as pneumatic air and passed through an overboard venturi/ejector assembly to produce a low pressure vacuum. This vacuum holds the safety valve open until take off.    On take-off, the dump solenoid closes and releases the compressor bleed air vacuum which closes the safety valve.  The preset solenoid opens and a time delay relay is actuated which allows the left engine to commence pressurization sequencing six seconds before the  right. The time delay prevents an excessive pressure bump. A pressure bump occurs when the aircraft pressurizes too quickly. ","roles":{"textData":{}}},{"id":"Image_2132","class":"TODO::Senthil","instance":"Image_2132","roles":{"click":{"subtype":"button"},"question":{"interactionId":"","quizId":-1,"text":"Image ","type":"graded","interactionType":"choice","score":{"weight":1,"penalty":0}},"textData":{}}},{"id":"Slide108119","class":"Normal Slide","instance":"t02p036","thumbnail":"","children":["si159182","Click_Box_388","Text_Caption_4814","Image_2132","Widget_22"],"roles":{"slide":{"durationInFrames":90},"navigation":{"navid":"Slide108119"}}},{"id":"si158850","class":"TODO::Senthil","roles":{"click":{"subtype":"button"},"question":{"interactionId":"183235","quizId":-1,"text":"Image ","type":"graded","interactionType":"choice","score":{"weight":1,"penalty":0}},"textData":{}}},{"id":"Click_Box_389","class":"TODO::Senthil","instance":"Click_Box_389","roles":{"click":{"subtype":"button"}}},{"id":"Text_Caption_6151","class":"TODO::Senthil","instance":"Text_Caption_6151","title":"Operation   The flow control unit then mixes engine bleed and ambient air.   The mixture of engine bleed and ambient air will go through (to cool) or by-pass (for heat retention) a heat exchanger in the wing center section before entering the cabin.   As the aircraft climbs, the outflow valve begins modulating outflow of air in accordance with the cabin pressure  controller to maintain the selected rate of climb and cabin altitude until the maximum cabin differential of 4.7 psid is reached.   Once the maximum cabin pressure differential is reached, the outflow valve will release air to maintain the maximum cabin differential rather than the setting  of the cabin pressure controller. After  this point, the cabin altitude begins to climb at approximately the same rate as the aircraft. Compressor bleed air is available for pressurization, heating and ventilation of the T-44C cabin. This bleed air is  tapped off of the diffuser section just after the 4th stage compressor and prior to the combustion chamber. Because the bleed air is delivered to the cabin at a relatively constant rate, the  pressurization system controls the T-44C cabin pressure by controlling the outflow of air from the cabin through two (2) flow control valves (the outflow valve and the safety valve). It does three (3)  things:   Meters the outflow of cabin air in \tresponse to vacuum control forces from the controller. Contains a preadjusted relief valve set to ensure that the cabin differential does not exceed 4.7 psi. (This means, the cabin altitude cannot be higher than the aircraft altitude.)                                                                   ","roles":{"textData":{}}},{"id":"Image_2335","class":"TODO::Senthil","instance":"Image_2335","roles":{"click":{"subtype":"button"},"question":{"interactionId":"","quizId":-1,"text":"Image ","type":"graded","interactionType":"choice","score":{"weight":1,"penalty":0}},"textData":{}}},{"id":"Slide126171","class":"Normal Slide","instance":"t07p010","thumbnail":"","children":["si159094","Click_Box_579","Text_Caption_5543","Image_2335","Widget_22"],"roles":{"slide":{"durationInFrames":90},"navigation":{"navid":"Slide126171"}}},{"id":"si159096","class":"TODO::Senthil","roles":{"click":{"subtype":"button"},"question":{"interactionId":"183235","quizId":-1,"text":"Image ","type":"graded","interactionType":"choice","score":{"weight":1,"penalty":0}},"textData":{}}},{"id":"Click_Box_580","class":"TODO::Senthil","instance":"Click_Box_580","roles":{"click":{"subtype":"button"}}},{"id":"Text_Caption_5544","class":"TODO::Senthil","instance":"Text_Caption_5544","title":"Safety Valve   The safety valve is also located on the aft pressure bulkhead near the outflow valve.   The safety valve is connected to the cabin pressure control switch and is wired through the left landing gear squat switch.   When the control switch is set to DUMP (or the LH squat switch is down and the switch is set to PRESS), the safety valve serves as a dump valve. This means it completely opens to relieve all the pressure differential between the external air pressure and the cabin air pressure. So, for smoke and fume elimination, going to dump would allow ram scoop ambient air to flow rhrough the cabin, flushing the fumes out via the safety valve.   A second function of the safety valve is to back up the outflow valve. The safety valve also contains a preadjusted relief valve. This valve is set to ensure that differential pressure does not exceed 4.9 psi. (Careful, this is easy to confuse with the preadjusted valve in the outflow valve.) After the engine(s) are started, the compressor bleed air is tapped off  the manifold at a T-fitting as pneumatic air and passed through an overboard venturi /ejector assembly to produce a low pressure vacuum. This vacuum holds the safety valve open until take off.  On take-off, the dump solenoid closes and releases the compressor bleed air vacuum which closes the safety valve.  The preset solenoid opens and a time delay relay is actuated which allows the left engine to commence pressurization sequencing six seconds before the  right. The time delay prevents an excessive pressure bump. A pressure bump occurs when the aircraft pressurizes too quickly. The mixture of engine bleed and ambient air will go through (to cool) or by-pass (for heat retention) a heat exchanger in the wing center section before entering the cabin.   As the aircraft climbs, the outflow valve begins modulating outflow of air in accordance with the cabin pressure  controller to maintain the selected rate of climb and cabin altitude until the maximum cabin differential of 4.7 psid is reached.   Once the maximum cabin pressure differential is reached, the outflow valve  will release air to maintain the maximum cabin differential rather than the setting  of the cabin pressure controller. After  this point, the cabin altitude begins to  climb at approximately the same rate as  the aircraft. The switch has three (3) positions: GRD MAX, NORM, and OFF.   When in the GRD MAX position and the aircraft is on the ground, the system uses eight (8) heating  elements to provide the maximum amount of electrical heat. This setting is used to initially warm up the cabin.   However, the switch is electrically held in the GRD MAX position. Once the aircraft takes off, the switch will automatically drop to NORM because the left squat switch de-energizes the  solenoid on liftoff.   In the NORM position, up to four (4) heating elements are automatically turned on and off in conjunction with the cabin thermostat to supplement bleed air heating.   In the OFF position, all electric heat is turned off and cabin heating is solely provided by bleed air. A full cylinder contains oxygen at a pressure  of 1850 psi (+/- 50 psi) at a temperature  of 70 degrees Fahrenheit.  Pressure Regulator Control Valve:   Connected to the oxygen supply  cylinder is the pressure regulator control valve. This valve is controlled by a remote push-pull knob located on the overhead panel in the cockpit. The pilot controls the propeller deicing boots with the propeller heat switch. The switch is placarded PROP and is located on the right hand pilot subpanel. ","roles":{"textData":{}}},{"id":"Image_2478","class":"TODO::Senthil","instance":"Image_2478","roles":{"click":{"subtype":"button"},"question":{"interactionId":"","quizId":-1,"text":"Image ","type":"graded","interactionType":"choice","score":{"weight":1,"penalty":0}},"textData":{}}},{"id":"Slide127901","class":"Normal Slide","instance":"t07p047","thumbnail":"","children":["si159252","Click_Box_619","Text_Caption_5589","Image_2478","Widget_22"],"roles":{"slide":{"durationInFrames":90},"navigation":{"navid":"Slide127901"}}},{"id":"si159148","class":"TODO::Senthil","roles":{"click":{"subtype":"button"},"question":{"interactionId":"183235","quizId":-1,"text":"Image ","type":"graded","interactionType":"choice","score":{"weight":1,"penalty":0}},"textData":{}}},{"id":"Click_Box_620","class":"TODO::Senthil","instance":"Click_Box_620","roles":{"click":{"subtype":"button"}}},{"id":"Text_Caption_5591","class":"TODO::Senthil","instance":"Text_Caption_5591","title":"Propeller Deicer Timer  The propeller deicer timer cycles power to the heating elements in this order:  RH propeller, outboard segments (all 3 blades)   RH propeller, inboard segments       (all 3 blades)  LH propeller, outboard segments       (all 3 blades)  LH propeller, inboard segments       (all 3 blades)  All above segments are heated 34 +/-6 seconds.
